<Name>Debra Wilson<//Name><Date>1576318089415<//Date><rating>5</rating>< review>
After visiting a couple other shops on Friday the 13th to check out the special flash, I was really unimpressed with pretty much everything. Bad customer service, boring designs.

When I walked into Electric Soul, I was greeted, I was welcomed, and I was encouraged to ask any questions I might have. I was immediately made comfortable.

They did have a piece of flash I liked, and after discussing the details with Danny, he got ready to put some ink on me. I laid down on the table and he cleaned my skin and placed the stencil, then had me stand to verify it was straight. Then he got to the fun part.

Overall it was a very good experience and I will go back in the future. Those other shops I visited first? They've lost a potential customer. I know days when they run specials can get crazy, but it's not hard to greet people and all what they're looking for.</review>

<Name>Justin Hudgins< /Name>< date>
1428370887224</date>
< Rate>
3</Rate>
< Review>
Tasty Chips and Salsa! Reminds me of Chevy's(for those familiar) with a bit more roasting to the peppers making for a nice smoky, spicy flavor that isn't going to burn your mouth.

I ordered the Enchiladas Banderas for $14.95 which comes with one Chili Verde enchilada, one ground beef, and one chicken. All three feature a different sauce on top. This plate is served with refried beans, Spanish rice, and sour cream.
I also ordered a cheese enchilada ala carte.(sadly they don't list any ala carte items or prices on their menu)

The Chili Verde was pretty good, but the ground beef and cheese were fantastic!
I could have done without the chicken enchilada. It was just pretty bland tasting.
The rice was very plain, but cooked nicely.
Same goes for the refried beans.

Beef tacos and cheese or beef enchiladas are a pricey $3.95 per ala carte item, with chicken, steak, and chili verde being $1 more.
A bit too much for the size IMO.(should be at least a dollar less)

$2.85 for a soda. I wouldn't know if that's fair these days because it's been a long time since I've ordered one while dining out.

Service was pretty good.

3 large flat screens in the bar area.

Happy Hour from 3-7pm.

They have a patio seating area adjacent the bar.

Pretty dirty carpeting for such a new restaurant. They need a good steam cleaning.(The carpet being shades of blue and beige probably doesn't help)</Review>

<user_name>j chen< /user_name>< Text>
Do yourself a favor and avoid anything service related with this establishment. I'm all for supporting hobby shops. There are few enough places where hobbiests can go to learn, share and expand their hobbying interests. Unfortunately Ventura hobbies as represented by its proprietor
Vernon Morseman, only hurts hobbiest.

I purchased rare $430 model steam locomotive from Vern with a "professionally installed sound, speed and light function controller". I discovered that the system was not completely installed and requested that the installer make all the advertised functions work. After 3 week delay, I was told that the train was broken and that it would need to be sent to the manufacturer for repair. The store would not pay for the repairs since he had no proof that the train was in working order when
it was received. "It was my word versus yours" as he put it. He also refused to pay for the return shipping of the model to me as previously promised when the train was dropped off. He wanted my cc number to pay for the return shipping. Having no further confidence in dealing with Ventura Hobbies, I ended up having to send someone 90 miles one way to pick it up for me. I was left with a broken out of production $430 item to sort out repairs for directly with the manufacture. It's taken several months and the unit is still not fully operable since the manufacture no longer makes the necessary parts.

Sob story aside, that's the level of service and commitment you can expect for premium priced purchase in excess of $400. Imagine the treatment you'll get when you take your child in with questions on their model or school project after you've already made the purchase.< /Text>

< Text>
If you're in Santa Monica you know you'll pay a premium for most meals and hotels generally push the margins pretty high. Why not go to a nook with a beautiful view by the beach that has excellent food in a stunningly elegant setting?  The wide conservatory look and feel with glass fluted light fixtures, tiled floor, tall ceilings, columns, expansive windows and spaciously spread out tables is worth a visit in its own right (the hotel was built in 1926).

Service is attentive and considerate, the food options are varied and everything served was well prepared. Not cheap but worth every penny.< /Text>

<review>(I'll preface this review by saying that I'd give Terrazza a 3.5 if I can, but it leans more toward a 4 within the limits of the system)

I came to Terrazza to meet up with some SoCal friends while I was in the area, and Santa Monica seemed like a great place to hang out! We stopped by on a weekend night, but we were still pretty easily able to find  a table in the open-seating area. The one downside about the open seating is that it's hard to get large groups (9+) to be able to sit together as they don't have many large tables.

The service is solid, we were asked how we were doing quite frequently, and drinks were replenished as we finished them. There's plenty of variety on the menu; beers, wines, mixed drinks, and food options. The view from the lounge area is great, and you can see lots of things taking place on the beach. The drinks are high quality and the food taste is on the same level. All the components of a great night!

There are a few complaints I have with the restaurant...parking can be really hard to find in the area, especially on a weekend night. One potential solution is to utilize the Valet parking at the hotel, but even with validation from the restaurant, it can get expensive if you're there for a few hours. The other major complaint boils down to the fact that you pay for the experience and not the food/drinks at this restaurant. This is probably to be expected at this level of establishment, but it's disappointing how little food you get for the price.

All told, I'd still recommend Terrazza, it's a great experience and a nice place to spend an evening with friends.< /review><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< response>
None< /response>

I‚Äôm between 2-3 stars on this because of my experience at a wedding here. Some family members got married here recently and I was very disappointed in the way this place acted as a venue and took advantage of the bride and groom. I can‚Äôt speak for it as a winery because this is my only experience here!
They rented the venue, but Toca was still open for wine tasting up until an hour before the start of the ceremony! There were strangers walking through our food tables, gifts and entire wedding set up all day and it was uncomfortable and frustrating since they had paid to rent the entire venue. (Which is also pretty ironic with their ‚Äúcovid safety‚Äù instructions they had on the doors that they would allow even more people in.)
Also, when we arrived in the morning to begin set up and getting ready, the inside was filthy. For ‚Äúcovid reasons‚Äù they would not allow us to use the indoor area for the wedding, but did not give any sort of discount. The bridal suit where we were able to get ready and hide our personal belongings from the other random people they had walking around, was actually so dirty. They had left stuff all over the counters that we just worked around and several of us swept the floors throughout the day because they were just that gross.
When we began taking photos outside behind the ceremony set up, we had to move several things out of the way that they had left in the grass & walkway including a pallet and an arbor.
To top it off, at the end of the evening they told us we had to have our arbor for the ceremony (not the one they left there) gone by 10am the next day- Easter Sunday. I wasn‚Äôt involved but my understanding was they had originally given several more days to get it since none of us had a truck.
It was a beautiful venue and wedding but honestly I‚Äôd have some hard conversations with these people before considering renting the venue and get all expectations in writing! And personally won‚Äôt be patronizing this place for wine tasting.
I‚Äôm mainly writing this for the viewing of the winery- to get their stuff together, do better as a business and treat people better. I‚Äôm sure many have had good experiences here- ours was just disappointing.<//review>

< Name>
Jesse M</Name>
< text>
Not worth it, overpriced and you can get better tacos from the taco truck a few blocks down for less.

The batter was burnt, and the overly sweet sauce they covered it with made it seem like I was eating a jelly doughnut wrapped in a tortilla.

Tacos are not meant to be sweet... For the love of everything holy, my hands are not supposed to be sticky after eating a taco!

I never thought you could mess up something so simple; the "unique" approach that they took to Mexican cuisine has made a mockery of it. It makes you question what person in their right mind greenlit the menu and thought Mexican food was missing turmeric rice and kale. I can honestly say I've had better Mexican food in West Virginia.

If you want overly priced food that will look pretty for your social media account, by all means, this is the place add a filter and watch the colors pop.

If you want savory food that isn't going to send you into diabetic shock, find a taco truck next to a construction site and enjoy some flavor.</text>

<rating>5< /rating>< review>
Don't let the hole-in-the-wall appearance fool you, this is gourmet restaurant quality food at an outstanding price. The incredible Mexican food coming out of this humble kitchen is shockingly good and surprisingly sophisticated. Expect a line, but know that it's worth every minute. (We pre-ordered and picked up an hour later.) I would trade a fancy restaurant setting for this incredible food every time. This is my go-to Mexican place in Los Angeles.<//review>

<review>We made a stop here for a quick, mildly cheap dinner, and we were thoroughly impressed by the quality of the tacos. They are a little more expensive than thought: if you're looking at the old menus, just know that the grilled and fried versions cost differently. The place had a very cute dining area with Spanish music playing, and we got our tacos fairly quickly. I was left quite full after two tacos, but managed to squeeze in a bite of the red velvet churros, which were pretty good. I wasn't expecting to detect that much of a difference between a normal churro and these flavored once, but I think they really nailed them! Definitely would recommend to friends near the UCLA area.</review>< pics>

<username>Jason Mckenzie< /username>< Review>
This place is legit. Sometimes there's a long wait but it's a hit or miss. I got 3 tacos, it was enough to fill me up. I got a kbbq taco, fried shrimp taco, and fried fish taco. The fried tacos were okay, maybe too fried got my taste, to be honest I think the quality of their food is so good that they don't need to fry it, and frying it actually made it worse. The grilled fish was a lot better than the fried.  Not the fanciest place but it's what you'd expect from a hole in the wall place. I will definitely be going back again. Great place for date night if your girl is chill and down for some amazing food and doesn't care about fine dining.

In summary, this place is legit, amazing food, but you gotta order right, I don't recommend the fried stuff, the grilled fish was great, and the KBBQ taco is my favorite.</Review>

<user>107417719605336789731<//user><name>Sidney Zakoni<//name>< date>
1568045910292</date>
<Rate>4</Rate><Text>Steamrolling up Westwood Blvd. at 10 mph over the speed limit to get home to watch a ball game I really wanted to see, my wife catches this small hut out of the corner of her eye and tells me to U-Turn it cuz she really feels like "Mexican Street food".
Well, coming from the Happy Wife / Happy Life school of matrimony, I obeyed. I mean it was the last thing on Earth I felt like but.........

Taco's Tu Madre looked like it would fit comfortably in Tijuana, Mexico City or just about any Pueblo south of the border. The only difference was there was a lot of people waiting to order. My first thought was "Well, what do we have here"? I mean I never heard of this place, let alone ever seen it, but, when you see this many people paying their money to get their food - Amen!

My crispy shrimp bowl with sweet and sour sauce mixed in kale was really really good. My wife order the three street tacos they make (of course) which she really enjoyed. A Pacifico or Modelo would have kicked this impromptu dinner through the roof, but alas I don't think the Beer and Wine Licensing people would give a hut a license.

This U-Turn just goes to show you, when you least expect it, you catch a winner.</Text>< Pics>

< Text>
Went here in late August, 2018 and was really disappointed in what's happened to this place.

- Prices went up
- Food quality declined
- The already long wait got longer

They had the best burritos and tacos in Westwood (some of the best in all of West LA), and I'm assuming they're under new management, as the decline in their quality and rise in their prices links up perfectly with them giving this place an unnecessary facelift (a couple neon signs, some window decals, and some signage plugging their social media). The wait had never been great here, but I always chalked that up to the undersized kitchen they're working with, and it was more than made up for by how good the food was. Now, the wait is significantly longer (there were multiple customers who had to check in to make sure their food was still coming out) for drastically worse food, at a higher price.

Really bummed to see them focus on changing things that didn't need to be changed and sacrificing what made this place great in the process.< /Text>

<rating>3< /rating><Time>1452382095173<//Time><gmap_id>0x80c2bb9c69a8d893:0x7ba8cea58a74bd57< /gmap_id><review>Bella Pita has been converted to a hip new taco stand with contemporary taco combinations. They have standard asada, pollo, but also fish and even duck. I came here from brunch and thought the tacos were just average and too small to justify the price.

I tried the egg and chorizo taco, as well as a chicken and guacamole. The presentation was okay, but the food itself was underwhelming. I think the meat from both tacos could have fit on a single tablespoon. The flavors were ok, but I was left unsatisfied with two tacos.

I also ordered red velvet churros for dessert, and they were better than the tacos. It came in 5 bite sized pieces with cream cheese filling and whipped cream.

Although they attempt to be hip and new, a taco is best when its simpler- and I'd rather have it from a truck or an establishment where they have perfected a few simple taco items.<//review>< Resp>
